			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Catherine Zeta-Jones</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><span class="fn">Catherine Zeta-Jones<br />
<small><a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></small></span></th>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Catherine Zeta-Jones VF 2012 Shankbone 2.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg/220px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg" width="220" height="275" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg/330px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg/440px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_VF_2012_Shankbone_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1690" data-file-height="2113" /></a>

<p><b>Catherine Zeta-Jones</b>, <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">CBE</a> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born 25 September 1969)<sup id="cite_ref-A_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A-1">[a]</a></sup> is a Welsh actress. Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>, Zeta-Jones aspired to be an actress from a young age. As a child, she played roles in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> productions of the musicals <i><a href="/wiki/Annie_(musical)" title="Annie (musical)">Annie</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bugsy_Malone" title="Bugsy Malone">Bugsy Malone</a></i>. She studied musical theatre at the <a href="/wiki/Arts_Educational_Schools,_London" title="Arts Educational Schools, London">Arts Educational Schools, London</a>, and made her stage breakthrough with a leading role in a 1987 production of <i><a href="/wiki/42nd_Street_(musical)" title="42nd Street (musical)">42nd Street</a></i>. Her screen debut came in the unsuccessful French-Italian film <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Nights_(film)" title="1001 Nights (film)">1001 Nights</a></i> (1990), and she went on to find greater success as a regular in the British television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Darling_Buds_of_May_(TV_series)" title="The Darling Buds of May (TV series)">The Darling Buds of May</a></i> (1991–93). Dismayed at being <a href="/wiki/Typecasting_(acting)" title="Typecasting (acting)">typecast</a> as the token pretty girl in British films, Zeta-Jones relocated to Los Angeles.</p>
<p>Zeta-Jones initially established herself in Hollywood with roles that highlighted her sex appeal such as in the action film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mask_of_Zorro" title="The Mask of Zorro">The Mask of Zorro</a></i> (1998) and the heist film <i><a href="/wiki/Entrapment_(film)" title="Entrapment (film)">Entrapment</a></i> (1999). Critics praised her portrayal of a vengeful pregnant woman in <i><a href="/wiki/Traffic_(2000_film)" title="Traffic (2000 film)">Traffic</a></i> (2000) and a murderous singer in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_(2002_film)" title="Chicago (2002 film)">Chicago</a></i> (2002). The latter won her <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">BAFTA</a> Awards for Best Supporting Actress, among other accolades. She starred in high-profile films for much of the decade, including the black comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Intolerable_Cruelty" title="Intolerable Cruelty">Intolerable Cruelty</a></i> (2003), the heist film <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Twelve" title="Ocean's Twelve">Ocean's Twelve</a></i> (2004), the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terminal" title="The Terminal">The Terminal</a></i> (2004), and the romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/No_Reservations_(film)" title="No Reservations (film)">No Reservations</a></i> (2007). Parts in smaller-scale features were followed by a decrease in workload, during which she returned to stage and portrayed an ageing actress in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Night_Music" title="A Little Night Music">A Little Night Music</a></i> (2009), winning a <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Actress in a Musical">Tony Award</a>. Zeta-Jones continued to work intermittently in the 2010s, starring in the psychological thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Side_Effects_(2013_film)" title="Side Effects (2013 film)">Side Effects</a></i> (2013) and the action film <i><a href="/wiki/Red_2_(film)" title="Red 2 (film)">Red 2</a></i> (2013).</p>
<p>Zeta-Jones is the recipient of <a href="/wiki/List_of_roles_and_awards_of_Catherine_Zeta-Jones#Awards_and_nominations" title="List of roles and awards of Catherine Zeta-Jones">several accolades</a>, including an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy Film Award">British Academy Film Award</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a>, and in 2010 she was appointed <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) for her film and humanitarian endeavours. She supports various charities and causes, and is a prominent celebrity endorser of brands. Her struggle with <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depression</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_II_disorder" title="Bipolar II disorder">bipolar II disorder</a> has been well documented by the media. She is married to the actor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas">Michael Douglas</a> with whom she has two children.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_initial_stage_career">Early life and initial stage career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg/220px-Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg/330px-Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg/440px-Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="563" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbles_wales_750px.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The district of <a href="/wiki/Mumbles_(district)" title="Mumbles (district)">Mumbles</a>, where Zeta-Jones was raised</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Zeta-Jones was born in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>, Wales, on 25 September 1969 to David Jones, the owner of a sweet factory, and his wife Patricia (<a href="/wiki/Given_name#Name_at_birth" title="Given name">née</a> Fair), a <a href="/wiki/Seamstress" class="mw-redirect" title="Seamstress">seamstress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-valley_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-valley-3">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> Her father is <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> and her mother is of <a href="/wiki/Irish_Catholic" title="Irish Catholic">Irish Catholic</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-season_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season-5">[4]</a></sup> She was named after her grandmothers, Zeta Jones and Catherine Fair.<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup> She has an older brother, David, and a younger brother, Lyndon, who worked as a sales representative before venturing into film production.<sup id="cite_ref-people_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people-7">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mumbles_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mumbles-8">[7]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones was raised in the suburban area of <a href="/wiki/Mumbles_(district)" title="Mumbles (district)">Mumbles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> Because Zeta-Jones was a hyperactive child, her mother sent her to the Hazel Johnson School of Dance when she was four years old.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-11">[10]</a></sup> She was educated at the <a href="/wiki/Dumbarton_House_School" title="Dumbarton House School">Dumbarton House School</a>, a private school in Swansea.<sup id="cite_ref-people_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people-7">[6]</a></sup> The family came from a modest background, but their fortunes improved when they won £100,000 in a <a href="/wiki/Bingo_(United_Kingdom)" title="Bingo (United Kingdom)">bingo</a> competition, allowing them to pay for Zeta-Jones' dance and ballet lessons.<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zeta-Jones participated in school stage shows from a young age and gained local media attention when her rendition of a <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Bassey" title="Shirley Bassey">Shirley Bassey</a> song won a Junior Star Trail talent competition.<sup id="cite_ref-frog_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frog-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> As part of a dance troupe, she routinely took trips to London, where she auditioned for roles in the theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-usaweekend_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaweekend-14">[13]</a></sup> At the age of nine, she was selected to play one of the orphan girls in a <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> production of the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Annie_(musical)" title="Annie (musical)">Annie</a></i>, and in her early teens, she became a national <a href="/wiki/Tap-dancing" class="mw-redirect" title="Tap-dancing">tap-dancing</a> champion.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-frog_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frog-12">[11]</a></sup> In 1981 she played the lead role of <a href="/wiki/Little_Orphan_Annie#Characters" title="Little Orphan Annie">Annie</a> in a Swansea production of the musical, which was staged at the <a href="/wiki/Swansea_Grand_Theatre" title="Swansea Grand Theatre">Swansea Grand Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-valley_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-valley-3">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup> Two years later, she played the lead role of Tallulah in a West End production of <i><a href="/wiki/Bugsy_Malone" title="Bugsy Malone">Bugsy Malone</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-frog_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frog-12">[11]</a></sup> When she was 15, Zeta-Jones dropped out of school without obtaining <a href="/wiki/O-levels" class="mw-redirect" title="O-levels">O-levels</a> and decided to live in London to pursue a full-time acting career; she was also engaged to perform in a touring production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pajama_Game" title="The Pajama Game">The Pajama Game</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-frog_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frog-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Describing her teenage years in London, Zeta-Jones said, "I would queue up for auditions and then change my costume or put on a different leotard and audition again. It might take me two tries, but I always got the job. I figured out what they wanted".<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-11">[10]</a></sup> She went on to attend the independent <a href="/wiki/Arts_Educational_Schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Arts Educational Schools">Arts Educational Schools</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chiswick" title="Chiswick">Chiswick</a>, London, for a three-year course in <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bio_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1987, when she was 17 years old, Zeta-Jones was picked as the second understudy to the lead actress in a West End production of <i><a href="/wiki/42nd_Street_(musical)" title="42nd Street (musical)">42nd Street</a></i>. During one of the performances, both the star and the first understudy were unavailable, and Zeta-Jones was asked to play the role of Peggy Sawyer—a chorus girl who becomes a star. The producer was impressed by her acting ability and allowed her to play the role for the next two years.<sup id="cite_ref-season_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season-5">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Communications1998_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Communications1998-18">[17]</a></sup> Her next stage appearance was with the <a href="/wiki/English_National_Opera" title="English National Opera">English National Opera</a> at the <a href="/wiki/London_Coliseum" title="London Coliseum">London Coliseum</a> in 1989 where she played Mae Jones in <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Weill" title="Kurt Weill">Kurt Weill</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Street_Scene_(opera)" title="Street Scene (opera)">Street Scene</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-bio_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hischak2008_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hischak2008-19">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1990–1996:_Screen_debut_and_career_struggles"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990.E2.80.931996:_Screen_debut_and_career_struggles">1990–1996: Screen debut and career struggles</span></h3>
<p>In 1990, Zeta-Jones made her film debut in the director <a href="/wiki/Philippe_de_Broca" title="Philippe de Broca">Philippe de Broca</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Nights_(film)" title="1001 Nights (film)">1001 Nights</a></i>. An adaptation of the Persian fable <i><a href="/wiki/One_Thousand_and_One_Nights" title="One Thousand and One Nights">One Thousand and One Nights</a></i>, the French-Italian production recounts the tale from the perspective of <a href="/wiki/Scheherazade" title="Scheherazade">Scheherazade</a> (Zeta-Jones), one of the brides of King Sharir (<a href="/wiki/Thierry_Lhermitte" title="Thierry Lhermitte">Thierry Lhermitte</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ZipesZipes2015_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZipesZipes2015-20">[19]</a></sup> The film was not well received at the box office, and according to de Broca's obituary in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>, the film "is best remembered for its enjoyable nude scenes".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Greater success followed when she starred opposite <a href="/wiki/David_Jason" title="David Jason">David Jason</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pam_Ferris" title="Pam Ferris">Pam Ferris</a> in the British period comedy-drama television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Darling_Buds_of_May_(TV_series)" title="The Darling Buds of May (TV series)">The Darling Buds of May</a></i> from 1991 to 1993. Adapted from <a href="/wiki/H._E._Bates" title="H. E. Bates">H.&#160;E. Bates</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> <a href="/wiki/The_Darling_Buds_of_May_(novel)" title="The Darling Buds of May (novel)">novel of the same name</a>, Zeta-Jones played the role of the eldest daughter of a family living in the countryside in 1950s Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-season_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season-5">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-face_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-face-22">[21]</a></sup> The series was the highest-rated television show in the country at the time, and Zeta-Jones gained wide public recognition for it; she said, "Literally, with one hour of television my life completely changed. I couldn't go anywhere".<sup id="cite_ref-usaweekend_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaweekend-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ButzelLopez1994_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ButzelLopez1994-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following a brief appearance as <a href="/wiki/Beatriz_Enr%C3%ADquez_de_Arana" title="Beatriz Enríquez de Arana">Beatriz Enríquez de Arana</a> in the unsuccessful adventure film <i><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus:_The_Discovery" title="Christopher Columbus: The Discovery">Christopher Columbus: The Discovery</a></i> (1992),<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones featured as a belly dancer in disguise in a 1992 episode of <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Young_Indiana_Jones_Chronicles" title="The Young Indiana Jones Chronicles">The Young Indiana Jones Chronicles</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> She next took on the part of an aspiring duchess in <i><a href="/wiki/Splitting_Heirs" title="Splitting Heirs">Splitting Heirs</a></i> (1993), a farcical period drama from the director <a href="/wiki/Robert_Young_(director)" title="Robert Young (director)">Robert Young</a> about two children (<a href="/wiki/Eric_Idle" title="Eric Idle">Eric Idle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Moranis" title="Rick Moranis">Rick Moranis</a>) who are separated at birth. Reviews for the film were negative, though the critic <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Canby" title="Vincent Canby">Vincent Canby</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> found her to be "very funny".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In 1994, Zeta-Jones played the melancholic Eustacia Vye in the television film <i>The Return of the Native</i>, an adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_the_Native" title="The Return of the Native">novel of the same name</a> (1878) by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy">Thomas Hardy</a>, and the wife of <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Owen" title="Lloyd Owen">Lloyd Owen</a>'s character in the television war drama <i>The Cinder Path</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Goble1999_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goble1999-29">[28]</a></sup> She was then cast as the <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">eponymous protagonist</a> of the 1995 television biopic <i><a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great_(1995_film)" title="Catherine the Great (1995 film)">Catherine the Great</a></i>. In a mixed review, critic Lisa Nesselson of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> found the miniseries to be "brightly colored" but "wooden and hollow", though thought that Zeta-Jones "imparts a certain grace and resolve to her sovereign-in-the-making".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones next starred as the pragmatic girlfriend of <a href="/wiki/Sean_Pertwee" title="Sean Pertwee">Sean Pertwee</a>'s character in <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Juice" title="Blue Juice">Blue Juice</a></i> (1995), publicised as Britain's first <a href="/wiki/Surf_film" title="Surf film">surf film</a>, which the critic <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Maltin" title="Leonard Maltin">Leonard Maltin</a> described as a "superficial and predictable" production.<sup id="cite_ref-Maltin2014_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maltin2014-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dismayed at being <a href="/wiki/Typecasting_(acting)" title="Typecasting (acting)">typecast</a> as the token pretty girl in British films, Zeta-Jones relocated to Los Angeles. She remarked, "There was all this fuss about who I was and wasn't dating. I was a pretty face and a big bust and nothing else. People in the business believed what they read about me. So I decided to move away and start again."<sup id="cite_ref-pretty_face_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pretty_face-33">[32]</a></sup> She believed that the anonymity she faced in America helped her get roles on merit and not due to her public image.<sup id="cite_ref-usaweekend_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaweekend-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pretty_face_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pretty_face-33">[32]</a></sup> She earned the part of Sala, the hench-woman to the villainous Drax (<a href="/wiki/Treat_Williams" title="Treat Williams">Treat Williams</a>) in the superhero film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_(1996_film)" title="The Phantom (1996 film)">The Phantom</a></i> (1996), starring <a href="/wiki/Billy_Zane" title="Billy Zane">Billy Zane</a> in the titular role.<sup id="cite_ref-Muir2004_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muir2004-34">[33]</a></sup> A reviewer for <i>Variety</i> considered Zeta-Jones to be a standout in her part, but the film received a negative critical reception and earned little at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-Muir2004_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muir2004-34">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> television miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1996_miniseries)" title="Titanic (1996 miniseries)">Titanic</a></i> (1996), however, was better received.<sup id="cite_ref-pretty_face_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pretty_face-33">[32]</a></sup> Starring opposite <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gallagher" title="Peter Gallagher">Peter Gallagher</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_C._Scott" title="George C. Scott">George C. Scott</a>, she portrayed the lead role of Isabella Paradine, a young mother engaged in an extramarital affair on the <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">RMS&#160;<i>Titanic</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Anderson2005_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson2005-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="1998–2000:_Hollywood_breakthrough_and_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998.E2.80.932000:_Hollywood_breakthrough_and_success">1998–2000: Hollywood breakthrough and success</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg/180px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg" width="180" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg/270px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="336" data-file-height="563" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Cannes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zeta-Jones at the premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Entrapment_(film)" title="Entrapment (film)">Entrapment</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/1999_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="1999 Cannes Film Festival">52nd Cannes Film Festival</a> in 1999</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> took notice of Zeta-Jones in <i>Titanic</i> and recommended her to <a href="/wiki/Martin_Campbell" title="Martin Campbell">Martin Campbell</a>, who was directing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mask_of_Zorro" title="The Mask of Zorro">The Mask of Zorro</a></i> (1998) for Spielberg's production company. Campbell cast her as the leading lady in favour of <a href="/wiki/Izabella_Scorupco" title="Izabella Scorupco">Izabella Scorupco</a>, who was his original choice for the part.<sup id="cite_ref-zorro_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zorro-37">[36]</a></sup> Co-starring <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Hopkins" title="Anthony Hopkins">Anthony Hopkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Banderas" title="Antonio Banderas">Antonio Banderas</a>, the film tells the story of <a href="/wiki/Zorro" title="Zorro">Zorro</a> (Hopkins), a Latin warrior who sets out to avenge the death of his wife and find his lost daughter Elena (Zeta-Jones). She found similarities between her "volatile" Celtic personality and her Latin character's temperament, and in preparation she studied dancing, riding and sword-fighting, and took diction lessons in Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Filming the action and dance sequences while wearing heavy corsets in the humid Mexican desert proved to be a challenge for Zeta-Jones, but she found the experience "worth suffering for".<sup id="cite_ref-zorro_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zorro-37">[36]</a></sup> <i>The Mask of Zorro</i> was positively received by the critics and earned over US$250 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> The role proved to be a breakthrough for her and she was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award_for_Best_Breakthrough_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Movie Award for Best Breakthrough Performance">MTV Movie Award for Best Breakthrough Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign-42">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zeta-Jones' first release of 1999 was the <a href="/wiki/Heist_film" title="Heist film">heist film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Entrapment_(film)" title="Entrapment (film)">Entrapment</a></i>, in which she starred opposite <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> as a seductive insurance agent on the lookout for an art thief. Despite a negative critical reception, the film was a commercial success;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Janet_Maslin" title="Janet Maslin">Janet Maslin</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> thought that the film provided Zeta-Jones a platform to "show off her slithery skills", and Desson Howe of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> called on viewers to appreciate the sex appeal she brought to the role.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Later that year, Zeta-Jones appeared alongside <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lili_Taylor" title="Lili Taylor">Lili Taylor</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Haunting_(1999_film)" title="The Haunting (1999 film)">The Haunting</a></i>, a remake of the <a href="/wiki/The_Haunting_(1963_film)" title="The Haunting (1963 film)">1963 film of the same name</a> about a team of paranormal experts who look into strange occurrences in an ill-fated mansion. The horror feature received generally poor reviews but found a significant worldwide audience.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> In a scathing review, the critic <a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle">Mick LaSalle</a> wrote that "Zeta-Jones seems less an actress and more a pretty face, and not an interesting one at that".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>After taking the supporting part of star <a href="/wiki/John_Cusack" title="John Cusack">John Cusack</a>'s romantic interest in the comedy-drama <i><a href="/wiki/High_Fidelity_(film)" title="High Fidelity (film)">High Fidelity</a></i> (2000), Zeta-Jones starred in <a href="/wiki/Steven_Soderbergh" title="Steven Soderbergh">Steven Soderbergh</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Traffic_(2000_film)" title="Traffic (2000 film)">Traffic</a></i> (2000).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> In the ensemble thriller on drug abuse starring <a href="/wiki/Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas">Michael Douglas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benicio_del_Toro" title="Benicio del Toro">Benicio del Toro</a>, she played Helena Ayala, the pregnant wife of a <a href="/wiki/Drug_lord" title="Drug lord">drug lord</a> who takes over the business when her husband is arrested. Initially written by Soderbergh as a mother of two, he changed the part to that of a pregnant woman on Zeta-Jones' suggestion, to accommodate her own pregnancy.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> Highly profitable at the box office and critically acclaimed,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> <i>Traffic</i> was described by the <i><a href="/wiki/Dallas_Observer" title="Dallas Observer">Dallas Observer</a></i> as "a remarkable achievement in filmmaking, a beautiful and brutal work".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Edward Guthman of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> found Zeta-Jones to be a standout among the ensemble and labelled her "sensational" in a scene in which she confronts a <a href="/wiki/Tijuana" title="Tijuana">Tijuana</a> dealer, adding that "through sheer conviction, she electrifies a moment that could have been absurd".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> The ensemble of <i>Traffic</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Cast_in_a_Motion_Picture" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Cast in a Motion Picture">SAG Award for Outstanding Cast</a> and Zeta-Jones was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actress – Motion Picture">Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hfp_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hfp-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2001–2004:_Chicago_and_other_roles"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001.E2.80.932004:_Chicago_and_other_roles">2001–2004: <i>Chicago</i> and other roles</span></h3>
<p>The romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Sweethearts" title="America's Sweethearts">America's Sweethearts</a></i> was Zeta-Jones' sole film project of 2001. She starred as a shrewd movie star, opposite <a href="/wiki/Julia_Roberts" title="Julia Roberts">Julia Roberts</a> who featured as her character's under-confident sibling. The critic <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> compared the film unfavourably to the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Singin%27_in_the_Rain" title="Singin' in the Rain">Singin' in the Rain</a></i> (1952), but thought that Zeta-Jones was aptly "chilly and manipulative" in her part.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> The following year, Zeta-Jones starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9e_Zellweger" title="Renée Zellweger">Renée Zellweger</a> as the murderous nightclub singer <a href="/wiki/Velma_Kelly" title="Velma Kelly">Velma Kelly</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_(2002_film)" title="Chicago (2002 film)">Chicago</a></i> (2002), a film adaptation of the Broadway musical of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_(musical)" title="Chicago (musical)">same name</a> from the director <a href="/wiki/Rob_Marshall" title="Rob Marshall">Rob Marshall</a>. She based her character's look and mannerisms on the actress <a href="/wiki/Louise_Brooks" title="Louise Brooks">Louise Brooks</a>, and as the script did not provide a backstory to Kelly, she worked to convey her character's "flamboyance" and "desperation" through "little looks and nuances".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> The film and her performance received critical acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> William Arnold of the <i><a href="/wiki/Seattle_Post-Intelligencer" title="Seattle Post-Intelligencer">Seattle Post-Intelligencer</a></i> felt that the actress made "a wonderfully statuesque and bitchy saloon goddess", and David Edelstein of <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> magazine wrote that she has "a smoldering confidence that takes your mind off her not-always-fluid dancing&#160;–&#160;although she's a perfectly fine hoofer, with majestic limbs and a commanding cleavage" and particularly praised her rendition of the song "<a href="/wiki/All_That_Jazz_(song)" title="All That Jazz (song)">All That Jazz</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> <i>Chicago</i> earned <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>306<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> worldwide, and was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Academy Award for Best Picture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> For her performance, Zeta-Jones won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Female_Actor_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Supporting Role">SAG Award</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">BAFTA Award</a> for Best Supporting Actress, among other awards and nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-singing_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singing-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the success of <i>Chicago</i>, Zeta-Jones voiced the part of Princess Marina in <i><a href="/wiki/Sinbad:_Legend_of_the_Seven_Seas" title="Sinbad: Legend of the Seven Seas">Sinbad: Legend of the Seven Seas</a></i> (2003), an animated film featuring <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a> as the voice of <a href="/wiki/Sinbad_the_Sailor" title="Sinbad the Sailor">Sinbad the Sailor</a>. She was drawn to the project to give her young children an opportunity to "hear [her] and get a sense of [her] on film",<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> although the film proved to be a <a href="/wiki/Box_office_bomb" title="Box office bomb">box office bomb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Also in 2003, Zeta-Jones starred alongside <a href="/wiki/George_Clooney" title="George Clooney">George Clooney</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Coen_Brothers" class="mw-redirect" title="Coen Brothers">Coen Brothers</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> black comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Intolerable_Cruelty" title="Intolerable Cruelty">Intolerable Cruelty</a></i>. A commercial success, the film saw her play the role of a serial divorcée who is drawn towards a divorce attorney (Clooney).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Writing for <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire magazine">Empire</a></i> magazine, the critic Damon Wise labelled the film a "dazzling screwball comedy" and felt that Zeta-Jones showed "an admirable facility for old-school quickfire patter".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> Other reviewers praised her onscreen chemistry with Clooney.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg/180px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg" width="180" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg/270px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg/360px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1364" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Feb05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zeta-Jones at the <a href="/wiki/Hasty_Pudding_Woman_of_the_Year" title="Hasty Pudding Woman of the Year">Hasty Pudding Woman of the Year</a> award ceremony in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2004, Spielberg approached her to play an insecure air hostess in his comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terminal" title="The Terminal">The Terminal</a></i>, a film about a man (<a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a>) who is trapped at the <a href="/wiki/JFK_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="JFK International Airport">JFK International Airport</a> when he is denied entry into the United States. Spielberg was intent on her playing against type as a strong-willed woman, with a vulnerability in her character,<sup id="cite_ref-usaweekend_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaweekend-14">[13]</a></sup> but the critic <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> felt that it came across as using her for "her looks rather than for the arch, self-mocking wit that is her secret weapon as a comic actress".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> Commercially, <i>The Terminal</i> performed well.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> She next worked with Soderbergh to film <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Twelve" title="Ocean's Twelve">Ocean's Twelve</a></i>, a sequel to his heist film <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Eleven_(2001_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ocean's Eleven (2001 film)">Ocean's Eleven</a></i> (2001), which also reunited her with stars Clooney, Pitt, and Roberts. The production, which was filmed in several countries across Europe, saw Zeta-Jones play Isabel Lahiri, a <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a> agent, and the love interest of Pitt's character.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Paul Clinton of <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> noted that her sex appeal benefited the film.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> Conversely, Ken Tucker of <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine argued that her character was redundant to the film's plot.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Despite dividing critics, the sequel earned over US$360 million globally.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2005–2010:_Decrease_in_workload_and_return_to_the_stage"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.932010:_Decrease_in_workload_and_return_to_the_stage">2005–2010: Decrease in workload and return to the stage</span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Zorro" title="The Legend of Zorro">The Legend of Zorro</a></i> (2005), a sequel to <i>The Mask of Zorro</i>, saw Zeta-Jones reprise her role of Eléna opposite Banderas. Set 10 years after the first film, the sequel follows Eléna struggling with married life.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign-42">[41]</a></sup> Unlike the original, the film was disliked by critics and was a commercial disappointment.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> She did not have any film releases in 2006. A biopic of <a href="/wiki/Harry_Houdini" title="Harry Houdini">Harry Houdini</a>, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Defying_Acts" title="Death Defying Acts">Death Defying Acts</a></i> (2007), starring <a href="/wiki/Guy_Pearce" title="Guy Pearce">Guy Pearce</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Escapologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Escapologist">escapologist</a> Houdini, featured Zeta-Jones as a Scottish con artist who claims psychic powers. The unsuccessful production was given only a limited theatrical release.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Zeta-Jones starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Eckhart" title="Aaron Eckhart">Aaron Eckhart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Breslin" title="Abigail Breslin">Abigail Breslin</a> in the romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/No_Reservations_(film)" title="No Reservations (film)">No Reservations</a></i>, a remake of the German film <i><a href="/wiki/Mostly_Martha_(film)" title="Mostly Martha (film)">Mostly Martha</a></i> (2001). <i>No Reservations</i> tells the story of an ambitious chef (Zeta-Jones) whose life changes for the better when she takes in her young niece (Breslin) after her sister's death. In preparation for her part, Zeta-Jones worked in the kitchen and waited on tables at New York's Fiamma Osteria restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Claudia Puig of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> thought that Zeta-Jones "shines as a character that finely balances off-putting reserve with sympathetic appeal", and Roger Ebert, despite disliking the film, found her "convincing" in her role.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> With a global gross of US$92 million, the film marked Zeta-Jones' final commercial success of the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following <i>No Reservations</i>, Zeta-Jones significantly decreased her workload in the next five years. She instead chose to focus on her family and health, having been diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_II_disorder" title="Bipolar II disorder">bipolar II disorder</a>, and her infrequent acting appearances were in smaller-scale and less successful productions.<sup id="cite_ref-czjinterview_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-czjinterview-89">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> She took on the role of a 40-year-old mother attracted to a younger man (<a href="/wiki/Justin_Bartha" title="Justin Bartha">Justin Bartha</a>) in the romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rebound" title="The Rebound">The Rebound</a></i>. The production was released theatrically in markets outside of the United States in 2009–10, but due to financial troubles of its distributor, The Film Development, the film failed to release theatrically in America.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_winning.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Catherine_winning.jpg/180px-Catherine_winning.jpg" width="180" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Catherine_winning.jpg/270px-Catherine_winning.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Catherine_winning.jpg/360px-Catherine_winning.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1087" data-file-height="1359" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_winning.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zeta-Jones at the <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk Award</a> ceremony in 2010, where she won <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award_for_Outstanding_Actress_in_a_Musical" title="Drama Desk Award for Outstanding Actress in a Musical">Outstanding Actress in a Musical</a> for her role in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Night_Music" title="A Little Night Music">A Little Night Music</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Zeta-Jones returned to stage in 2009 with a revival of the musical <i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Night_Music" title="A Little Night Music">A Little Night Music</a></i>, which marked her Broadway debut. Set in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> during the early twentieth century, the musical follows the relationship between three people (Zeta-Jones, <a href="/wiki/Angela_Lansbury" title="Angela Lansbury">Angela Lansbury</a> and Alexander Hanson) during the course of an evening. She played Desirée Armfeldt, an ageing actress, and was particularly drawn to the complexities of the play, saying, "There's no jazzy hands, no high kicks, no fishnet stockings,&#160;... It's not one of those shows where you can dig about three inches and come out the other end. You can keep digging and digging and digging".<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-11">[10]</a></sup> She did not listen to past recordings of the songs in the play so she could bring her own interpretation to them.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-11">[10]</a></sup> The critic Claire Prentice of <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> wrote that Zeta-Jones brought in a "quiet, reflective poignancy" in her rendition of the song "<a href="/wiki/Send_in_the_Clowns" class="mw-redirect" title="Send in the Clowns">Send in the Clowns</a>", but Emma Brocks of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> was more critical, remarking that "with her pretty voice, head wresting this way and that, [she] seems to be auditioning for stage school".<sup id="cite_ref-singing_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singing-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> For her performance, Zeta-Jones won the <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award_for_Outstanding_Actress_in_a_Musical" title="Drama Desk Award for Outstanding Actress in a Musical">Drama Desk Award for Outstanding Actress in a Musical</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Actress in a Musical">Tony Award for Best Actress in a Musical</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2012–present:_Return_to_film_and_television"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.93present:_Return_to_film_and_television">2012–present: Return to film and television</span></h3>
<p>Following a three-year sabbatical from acting, Zeta-Jones made her screen comeback in <i><a href="/wiki/Lay_the_Favorite" title="Lay the Favorite">Lay the Favorite</a></i> (2012), a comedy co-starring <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Willis" title="Bruce Willis">Bruce Willis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Hall" title="Rebecca Hall">Rebecca Hall</a>, in which she played the jealous wife of a gambler (Willis).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> Reviews for the film were negative, and the critic Betsy Sharkey of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> found Zeta-Jones to be "far too shrill to amuse".<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> In the ensemble musical comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Ages_(2012_film)" title="Rock of Ages (2012 film)">Rock of Ages</a></i>, co-starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise" title="Tom Cruise">Tom Cruise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Cranston" title="Bryan Cranston">Bryan Cranston</a>, Zeta-Jones played the part of a religiously conservative wife of a mayor. She was attracted to the idea of playing a "nightmare of a woman" and based the role on the politician <a href="/wiki/Michele_Bachmann" title="Michele Bachmann">Michele Bachmann</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-czjinterview_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-czjinterview-89">[88]</a></sup> the film received mixed reviews and failed commercially.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Her final release of 2012 was <i><a href="/wiki/Playing_for_Keeps_(2012_film)" title="Playing for Keeps (2012 film)">Playing for Keeps</a></i>, a romantic comedy with <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Butler" title="Gerard Butler">Gerard Butler</a>, which proved to be her third box office failure of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Zeta-Jones took on a leading role in the crime thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Broken_City_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Broken City (film)">Broken City</a></i>, co-starring <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe" title="Russell Crowe">Russell Crowe</a>. The film tells the story of a private detective (Wahlberg) who is hired by the mayor of New York (Crowe) to spy on his wife (Zeta-Jones). <a href="/wiki/Todd_McCarthy" title="Todd McCarthy">Todd McCarthy</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> thought that Zeta-Jones "looks like class itself and nicely underplays", and Liam Lacey of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail" title="The Globe and Mail">The Globe and Mail</a></i> observed that the actress "does a fair, if incongruous, impersonation of a forties vamp".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> However, as with Zeta-Jones' previous few projects, the film was not widely seen, and received poor reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> This changed when Zeta-Jones collaborated with Soderbergh for the third time to film the critically acclaimed thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Side_Effects_(2013_film)" title="Side Effects (2013 film)">Side Effects</a></i> (2013).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> Co-starring with <a href="/wiki/Channing_Tatum" title="Channing Tatum">Channing Tatum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jude_Law" title="Jude Law">Jude Law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rooney_Mara" title="Rooney Mara">Rooney Mara</a>, the film saw her play a mysterious psychiatrist who recommends an <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressant</a> drug with serious side effects. Peter Travers found the film to be a "hell of a thriller, twisty, terrific and packed with surprises" and considered Zeta-Jones to be "dynamite" in it.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the action-comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Red_2_(film)" title="Red 2 (film)">Red 2</a></i> (2013), which served as a sequel to the 2010 film <i><a href="/wiki/Red_(2010_film)" title="Red (2010 film)">Red</a></i>, Zeta-Jones played a seductive Russian double agent, alongside Bruce Willis, <a href="/wiki/Helen_Mirren" title="Helen Mirren">Helen Mirren</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mary-Louise_Parker" title="Mary-Louise Parker">Mary-Louise Parker</a>. She was drawn to the project, which follows the comic adventures of retired spies, for "the action, the humour, [and] the tongue-in-cheek quality of it".<sup id="cite_ref-torture_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-109">[108]</a></sup> Writing for <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i>, Justin Lowe remarked that Zeta-Jones "nicely pulls off Russian spy Katja's mix of allure and menace", and with a worldwide gross of US$148 million, <i>Red 2</i> emerged as her most widely seen film since <i>No Reservations</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following <i>Red 2</i>, Zeta-Jones took another sabbatical from acting, saying: "If I'm going to leave my family for any length of time it had better be for a role that I haven't played before, [otherwise] I would prefer to stay at home".<sup id="cite_ref-torture_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-109">[108]</a></sup> She found the role opposite <a href="/wiki/Bill_Nighy" title="Bill Nighy">Bill Nighy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toby_Jones" title="Toby Jones">Toby Jones</a> in the British war comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Dad%27s_Army_(2016_film)" title="Dad's Army (2016 film)">Dad's Army</a></i> (2016), based on the television sitcom of the <a href="/wiki/Dad%27s_Army" title="Dad's Army">same name</a>. She was cast as a glamorous journalist reporting on a British Home Guard platoon based in <a href="/wiki/Walmington-on-Sea" title="Walmington-on-Sea">Walmington-on-Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> Catherine Bray of <i>Variety</i> found the film to be an "amiable but creaky resurrection" of the popular sitcom, and thought that while Zeta-Jones "hits the required single note with some spirit" she was "generally underused" in it.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones returned to television the following year by portraying the actress <a href="/wiki/Olivia_de_Havilland" title="Olivia de Havilland">Olivia de Havilland</a> in the first season of <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Murphy_(writer)" title="Ryan Murphy (writer)">Ryan Murphy</a>'s anthology drama series <i><a href="/wiki/Feud_(TV_series)" title="Feud (TV series)">Feud</a></i>, subtitled <i>Bette and Joan</i>, about the rivalry between the actresses <a href="/wiki/Joan_Crawford" title="Joan Crawford">Joan Crawford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bette_Davis" title="Bette Davis">Bette Davis</a> (played by <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Lange" title="Jessica Lange">Jessica Lange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>, respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> Dominic Patten of <a href="/wiki/Deadline.com" title="Deadline.com">Deadline.com</a> found Zeta-Jones to be "wonderfully cast" and Sonia Saraiya of <i>Variety</i> praised her for providing "the best turn in the show".<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Displeased with her portrayal in the series, de Havilland, at 101 years old, sued the network and producers of <i>Feud</i> for <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_privacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of privacy">invasion of privacy</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Personality_rights" title="Personality rights">personality rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of June 2017, Zeta-Jones has commenced filming for <i>Cocaine Godmother</i>, a television biopic on the drug lord <a href="/wiki/Griselda_Blanco" title="Griselda Blanco">Griselda Blanco</a>, which will premiere in 2018 on <a href="/wiki/Lifetime_(TV_network)" title="Lifetime (TV network)">Lifetime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg/180px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg" width="180" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg/270px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg/360px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zeta-Jones in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to her acting career, Zeta-Jones supports various charities and causes. She is a patron of Swansea's Longfields Day Centre for the disabled, and has made sizeable donations to the centre.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> In 2001, she auctioned an outfit she wore in <i>The Mask of Zorro</i> (1998) to raise funds for <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in Africa">AIDS patients in Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> In 2005, she became the ambassador of the <a href="/wiki/National_Society_for_the_Prevention_of_Cruelty_to_Children" title="National Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children">National Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children</a> charity, and launched the Full Stop appeal in Wales to raise awareness on child abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> She has also given her support to other charitable organisations for children such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Missing_%26_Exploited_Children" title="International Centre for Missing &amp; Exploited Children">International Centre for Missing &amp; Exploited Children</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Noah%27s_Ark_Appeal" class="mw-redirect" title="Noah's Ark Appeal">Noah's Ark Appeal</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones is also the founding host for <i>A Fine Romance</i>, an annual charitable program that helps raise funds for the <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_%26_Television_Fund" title="Motion Picture &amp; Television Fund">Motion Picture &amp; Television Fund</a>, and is one of the members of the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_for_Peace_Foundation" title="Cinema for Peace Foundation">Cinema for Peace Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zeta-Jones briefly dabbled with a singing career in the early 1990s. In 1992, she provided her voice to the character of actress <a href="/wiki/Jean_Simmons" title="Jean Simmons">Jean Simmons</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Wayne" title="Jeff Wayne">Jeff Wayne</a>'s musical retelling of <i><a href="/wiki/Spartacus_(film)" title="Spartacus (film)">Spartacus</a></i>, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Wayne%27s_Musical_Version_of_Spartacus" title="Jeff Wayne's Musical Version of Spartacus">Jeff Wayne's Musical Version of Spartacus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> Three years later, she released her first single, "In the Arms of Love", on Wayne's Wow! Records.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> She later sang "<a href="/wiki/True_Love_Ways" title="True Love Ways">True Love Ways</a>", a duet with <a href="/wiki/David_Essex" title="David Essex">David Essex</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-Larkin2011_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larkin2011-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zeta-Jones has featured as an advertising spokeswoman for several brands and products. She was named the global ambassador for the cosmetics company <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Arden,_Inc." title="Elizabeth Arden, Inc.">Elizabeth Arden, Inc.</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> Also that year, she was signed on by the phone company <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a> for an estimated US$10 million per year, making her the highest-paid celebrity endorser at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> In 2017, Zeta-Jones launched her own line of home decoration products named Casa Zeta-Jones.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>The success of the television series <i>The Darling Buds of May</i> (1991–93) made Zeta-Jones a popular celebrity in Britain, and her personal life has since been chronicled by the media.<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup> Her relationships in the early 1990s with the television personality <a href="/wiki/John_Leslie_(TV_presenter)" title="John Leslie (TV presenter)">John Leslie</a>, the singer <a href="/wiki/David_Essex" title="David Essex">David Essex</a>, and the pop star <a href="/wiki/Mick_Hucknall" title="Mick Hucknall">Mick Hucknall</a> were widely reported by the British press.<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup> In the mid-1990s she was briefly engaged to the Scottish actor <a href="/wiki/Angus_Macfadyen" title="Angus Macfadyen">Angus Macfadyen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> In an interview with the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i> in 1995, she described her lifestyle: "I drink, I swear, I like sex".<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Zeta-Jones_Michael_Douglas_2012_Shankbone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zeta-Jones with husband <a href="/wiki/Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas">Michael Douglas</a> at the <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> party for the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Zeta-Jones met the actor Michael Douglas, with whom she shares a birthday and who is 25 years her senior, at the <a href="/wiki/Deauville_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Deauville Film Festival">Deauville Film Festival</a> in France in August 1998, after being introduced by <a href="/wiki/Danny_DeVito" title="Danny DeVito">Danny DeVito</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> They became engaged on 31 December 1999, and were married at the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Hotel" title="Plaza Hotel">Plaza Hotel</a> in New York on 18 November 2000 after Douglas' divorce was finalised.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> The high-profile ceremony, which cost an estimated £1.5 million, was labelled as the "wedding of the year" by the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-wedding_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wedding-138">[137]</a></sup> The couple signed a £1&#160;million deal with <i><a href="/wiki/OK!" title="OK!">OK!</a></i> magazine to release pictures of the event, and the rest of the press were not permitted to enter.<sup id="cite_ref-wedding_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wedding-138">[137]</a></sup> Despite this, journalists of <i><a href="/wiki/Hello!_(magazine)" title="Hello! (magazine)">Hello!</a></i> magazine surreptitiously took pictures of the ceremony, and the couple successfully sued the magazine for invasion of privacy.<sup id="cite_ref-wedding_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wedding-138">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Douglas and Zeta-Jones have two children, a son Dylan Michael (born August 2000)<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> and a daughter Carys Zeta (born April 2003).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> The family lived in <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> until 2009, and as of 2016, live in rural New York State.<sup id="cite_ref-torture_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> In 2010, Douglas was diagnosed with tongue cancer, and Zeta-Jones faced an emotionally turbulent time; she said, "When you get sideswiped like that [with the illness] it's an obvious trigger for your balance to be a little bit off – not sleeping, worry, stress."<sup id="cite_ref-torture_109-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-109">[108]</a></sup> This trigger led to Zeta-Jones suffering from <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depression</a>, and despite initial apprehension, she spoke publicly about suffering from <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_II_disorder" title="Bipolar II disorder">bipolar II disorder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-torture_109-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> She sought treatment by checking herself into hospital in 2011, and again in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-torture_109-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torture-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> Owing to the stress of both their illnesses, the couple decided to live separately in 2013, though without taking legal action towards separation or divorce.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> They reconciled in 2014, with Douglas stating that they were "stronger than ever".<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg/220px-Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg/330px-Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg/440px-Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1221" data-file-height="1232" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zeta-Jones_close-up.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zeta-Jones at a <a href="/wiki/Drama_League_of_New_York" title="Drama League of New York">Drama League</a> Benefit Gala in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Zeta-Jones' beauty and sex appeal has been picked up by several sources, including <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> magazine, who ranked her first in their listing of the "Most Beautiful People" in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-most_beautiful_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-most_beautiful-148">[147]</a></sup> She continued to feature in the list from 2000–04.<sup id="cite_ref-most_beautiful_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-most_beautiful-148">[147]</a></sup> In 2003, the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Esquire_(magazine)" title="Esquire (magazine)">Esquire</a></i> labelled her the most beautiful woman on the planet.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> In 2011, she was named the most beautiful British woman by a poll conducted by the television network <a href="/wiki/QVC" title="QVC">QVC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>The journalist Sheila Johnston of <i>The Daily Telegraph</i>, in 2010, described Zeta-Jones as "the ultimate self-made success" who "constantly made bold decisions, and scrubbed up very nicely into a luscious star who radiates a classic […] brand of big-screen glamour."<sup id="cite_ref-valley_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-valley-3">[2]</a></sup> Guy Adams of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> considers her personality to be "self-effacing and energetic" but takes note of her "steely core" in her off-screen persona.<sup id="cite_ref-steely_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steely-6">[5]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones' success in her early Hollywood films <i>The Mask of Zorro</i> (1998) and <i>Entrapment</i> (1999) relied predominantly on her sex appeal, but she was later appreciated for her versatility.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Communications1998_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Communications1998-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc2003_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2003-151">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zeta-Jones' career graph and marriage to Douglas has been a subject of satire. A 2006 episode of the satirical British television show <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Stories" title="Star Stories">Star Stories</a></i> (2006–2008) was entitled <i>Catherine Zeta-Jones&#160;— Her Quest to Prove Herself&#160;... And Also Find Love</i>, about a fictitious life story of Zeta-Jones.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> Addressing her perceived media image, Zeta-Jones remarked in a 2004 interview to <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Weekend" title="USA Weekend">USA Weekend</a></i>: "The biggest misconception of me is that I'm some die-hard, ambitious, do-anything-to-get-anything kind of person, I'm not. I'm very shy socially."<sup id="cite_ref-usaweekend_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaweekend-14">[13]</a></sup> Zeta-Jones is protective of her public image, and the use of her likeness is carefully controlled. As well as taking legal action against <i>Hello!</i> magazine, she sued a <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>-based topless club for including her image on their advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> In 2003, the celebrity biographer Cliff Goodwin wrote an unauthorised biography of the actress, entitled <i>Catherine Zeta Jones: The Biography</i>, but the publication was indefinitely postponed when she issued a legal notice prohibiting its release.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography_and_awards">Filmography and awards</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_roles_and_awards_of_Catherine_Zeta-Jones" title="List of roles and awards of Catherine Zeta-Jones">List of roles and awards of Catherine Zeta-Jones</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_filmography">Selected filmography</span></h3>
<p>Zeta-Jones' films that have earned the most at the box office, as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Catherine_Zeta-Jones&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, include:<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Mask_of_Zorro" title="The Mask of Zorro">The Mask of Zorro</a></i> (1998)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Entrapment_(film)" title="Entrapment (film)">Entrapment</a></i> (1999)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Haunting_(1999_film)" title="The Haunting (1999 film)">The Haunting</a></i> (1999)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Traffic_(2000_film)" title="Traffic (2000 film)">Traffic</a></i> (2000)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Sweethearts" title="America's Sweethearts">America's Sweethearts</a></i> (2001)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_(2002_film)" title="Chicago (2002 film)">Chicago</a></i> (2002)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Twelve" title="Ocean's Twelve">Ocean's Twelve</a></i> (2004)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Terminal" title="The Terminal">The Terminal</a></i> (2004)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/No_Reservations_(film)" title="No Reservations (film)">No Reservations</a></i> (2007)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Red_2_(film)" title="Red 2 (film)">Red 2</a></i> (2013)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span></h3>
<p>For her role in <i>Chicago</i> (2002), Zeta-Jones was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Female_Actor_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Supporting Role">SAG Award</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">BAFTA Award</a> for Best Supporting Actress.<sup id="cite_ref-singing_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singing-65">[64]</a></sup> She has received two <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> nominations: <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actress – Motion Picture">Best Supporting Actress</a> for <i>Traffic</i> (2000) and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Comedy_or_Musical" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Motion Picture Comedy or Musical">Best Actress in a Comedy or Musical</a> for <i>Chicago</i> (2002).<sup id="cite_ref-hfp_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hfp-58">[57]</a></sup> She was appointed <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">Monarchy of the United Kingdom</a> in <a href="/wiki/2010_Birthday_Honours" title="2010 Birthday Honours">2010</a> for her film and charity work.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="&quot;-moz-column-width:" id="cite_ref-A_1-1">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-A-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-A_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-A_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The name on her <a href="/wiki/Birth_certificate" title="Birth certificate">birth certificate</a> is Catherine Zeta Jones, without the hyphen.<sup id="cite_ref-valley_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-valley-3">[2]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">(2001–2009)</th>

<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">

<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Gosford_Park" title="Gosford Park">Gosford Park</a></b></i> (2001): <span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Eileen_Atkins" title="Eileen Atkins">Eileen Atkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Balaban" title="Bob Balaban">Bob Balaban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bates" title="Alan Bates">Alan Bates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dance" title="Charles Dance">Charles Dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gambon" title="Michael Gambon">Michael Gambon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Grant" title="Richard E. <li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Chicago_(2002_film)" title="Chicago (2002 film)">Chicago</a></b></i> (2002): <span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Christine_Baranski" title="Christine Baranski">Christine Baranski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ekaterina_Shchelkanova" title="Ekaterina Shchelkanova">Ekaterina Shchelkanova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taye_Diggs" title="Taye Diggs">Taye Diggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denise_Faye" title="Denise Faye">Denise Faye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colm_Feore" title="Colm Feore">Colm Feore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Gere" title="Richard Gere">Richard Gere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deidre_Goodwin" title="Deidre Goodwin">Deidre Goodwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Liu" title="Lucy Liu">Lucy Liu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Misner" title="Susan Misner">Susan Misner</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BDa" title="Mýa">Mýa</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_C._Reilly" title="John C. <th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">1951–1975</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
